Sectarian Views on the Companions and Preference of Ali over Abu Bakr
Survey of sectarian positions on the Companions and preference of Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse sectarian positions regarding the status of the Companions, particularly the preference of Ali over Abu Bakr, as reported by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Different sects held vastly different views on the Companions, but many later theologians favored Ali while affirming Abu Bakr.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a survey of the positions held by various Shi'a and Mu'tazili groups concerning the early Companions. It focuses on the question of whether Ali is superior to Abu Bakr and how different subsects of the Zaydiyya and Mu'tazila addressed this. Understanding these diverse views is essential for grasping later theological debates on the Imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get a sense of the different groups mentioned.
2
Identify the main groups
List the groups: Imamites, Jarudiyya, Juririyya, Ya'qubiyya, Mu'tazila (al-Ka'bi and al-Jubba'i).
Notice the order of presentation.
3
Focus on the Zaydi subsects
Notice the differences among the Zaydi subsects: Jarudiyya declare Abu Bakr kafir; Juririyya and Ya'qubiyya affirm his imamate but still prefer Ali.
4
Understand the Mu'tazili position
Learn that most later Mu'tazila, including al-Ka'bi, adopted the view of preferring Ali while affirming Abu Bakr and Umar, while al-Jubba'i was cautious.
Al-Jubba'i's conditional statement is important.
5
Reflect on the diversity
Consider why this diversity matters for the study of kalam and the development of Sunni orthodoxy.
This passage sets the stage for later refutations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الإمامية فأكثرهم على أن من سوى علي وابنيه وفاطمة ونفر يسير من الصحابة ارتدوا بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام، وكذا الجارودية من الزيدية يكفرون أبا بكر، فأما الجريرية من الزيدية وهم أصحاب سليمان بن جرير رؤساء الزيدية، فإنهم يثبتون إمامة أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما، ويكفرون الجارودية منهم في إكفارهم أبا بكر وعمر، وكذا اليعقوبية من الزيدية يتولون أبا بكر وعمر غير أنهم لا يتبرءون ممن تبرأ من أبي بكر وعمر، غير أن الجريرية واليعقوبية مع هذا يفضلون عليًا على جميع الصحابة، وإلى هذا يذهب أكثر متأخري المعتزلة، ونص الكعبي على اختياره هذا المذهب في كتابه المسمى بعيون المسائل، وأما الجبائي من جملة رؤساء المعتزلة فإنه كان يتوقف في ذلك وكان يقول: إن صح خبر الطير فعلي أفضل.
As for the Imamites, most of them hold that other than Ali, his two sons, Fatima, and a few of the Companions apostatized after the death of the Prophet peace be upon him. Likewise, the Jarudiyya of the Zaydiyya declare Abu Bakr to be an unbeliever. As for the Juririyya of the Zaydiyya, who are the followers of Sulayman ibn Jarir, the leaders of the Zaydiyya, they affirm the imamate of Abu Bakr and Umar may Allah be pleased with them, and they declare the Jarudiyya among them to be unbelievers because of their declaring Abu Bakr and Umar to be unbelievers. Likewise, the Ya'qubiyya of the Zaydiyya show loyalty to Abu Bakr and Umar, but they do not disavow those who disavow Abu Bakr and Umar. However, the Juririyya and Ya'qubiyya, despite this, prefer Ali over all the Companions. This is the view of most of the later Mu'tazila, and al-Ka'bi stated his choice of this doctrine in his book titled 'Uyun al-Masa'il. As for al-Jubba'i, among the leading Mu'tazila, he used to refrain from this matter and used to say: If the report of the bird is authentic, then Ali is superior.
Source pages p. 1186

Commentary
This passage lists the positions of various sects regarding the early Companions, particularly the status of Abu Bakr and Ali. The author begins with the Imamites (extreme Shi'a), who hold that most Companions apostatized after the Prophet's death, except for Ali, his sons, Fatima, and a few others. He then mentions the Jarudiyya, a Zaydi subsect that declares Abu Bakr an unbeliever. Next, the Juririyya, another Zaydi group following Sulayman ibn Jarir, affirm the imamate of Abu Bakr and Umar and declare the Jarudiyya unbelievers for their stance. Similarly, the Ya'qubiyya show loyalty to Abu Bakr and Umar but do not dissociate from those who disavow them. Despite this, both Juririyya and Ya'qubiyya prefer Ali over all Companions. The author notes that this view of preferring Ali while affirming Abu Bakr and Umar is adopted by most later Mu'tazila, and al-Ka'bi explicitly chose it in his book. Finally, al-Jubba'i, another Mu'tazili leader, used to refrain from this issue but indicated that if the hadith of the bird (concerning Ali's virtue) is authentic, then Ali is superior. This passage surveys the diversity of opinion without evaluating them yet.

الجارودية
الجريرية
اليعقوبية
المعتزلة
تفضيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Shi'a uniformly reject Abu Bakr
Correction: The passage shows variety among Zaydi subsects; some like the Juririyya and Ya'qubiyya affirm his imamate while still preferring Ali.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Zaydi subsect declares Abu Bakr an unbeliever?
A) The Jarudiyya
B) The Juririyya
C) The Ya'qubiyya
D) The Imamites

Key Takeaway
This passage illustrates the diverse range of opinions among early Islamic sects regarding the Companions, particularly the preference of Ali over Abu Bakr, with many later theologians adopting a middle position that affirms the first two caliphs while still favoring Ali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about these sects that went to extremes—declaring Companions unbelievers or apostates—does it make you examine your own heart: have you ever harbored resentment or ill feelings towards any Companion, even silently? How would you correct that before Allah?
?
The passage shows that affirming the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar while still preferring Ali was a considered position for many scholars. Do you approach these historical debates with the same intellectual humility, or do you simply follow the view of your community without weighing the evidence yourself?
?
Al-Jubba'i said: 'If the report of the bird is authentic, then Ali is superior.' That is a conditional statement. Are you ready to submit to truth wherever it leads, even if it means revising a long-held view about the Companions? Or do you cling to a position out of group loyalty rather than conviction?

The Quranic Evidence for Abu Bakr's Superiority from the Cave Verse
Interpretation of Quran 9:40 to argue Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse of the cave (9:40) is used to argue for Abu Bakr's superiority over all other Companions.

Core Idea
The cave verse uniquely honors Abu Bakr as the recipient of divine tranquility.

The passage begins by citing the famous verse about the Prophet and Abu Bakr in the cave during the Hijra. The author interprets the verse to highlight Abu Bakr's special status, arguing that the sending of tranquility was specifically for him. This lesson unpacks the tafsir and its implications for establishing Abu Bakr's superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its context
Read the Arabic verse and its translation. Note that it describes the Prophet's exile and his companion.
The verse is from Surah al-Tawbah.
2
Analyze the interpretation of 'companion'
The author emphasizes that Abu Bakr is explicitly called the Prophet's companion (sahib). This is a unique honor.
No other Companion is addressed personally in the Quran.
3
Understand the pronoun 'upon him'
The author argues that 'upon him' in 'Allah sent down His tranquility upon him' refers to Abu Bakr, not the Prophet, because the Prophet did not need tranquility.
This grammatical point is key to the argument.
4
Reflect on the special characteristics
The verse attributes to Abu Bakr being 'second of two' and chosen for companionship, which no other Companion possesses.
These are unique distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة على أفضلية الصديق: إِلَّا تَنصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللَّهُ إِذْ أَخْرَجَهُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ثَانِيَ اثْنَيْنِ إِذْ هُمَا فِي الْغَارِ إِذْ يَقُولُ لِصَاحِبِهِ لَا تَحْزَنْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَنَا فَأَنزَلَ اللَّهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَيْهِ (سورة التوبة ٩: ٤٠) في الآية أنه صاحب رسول الله عليه السلام، وأن الله نصره كما نصر نبيه حيث قال "إن الله معنا" أي بالنصر، ثم الهاء في قوله: فأنزل الله سكينته عليه عائدة إلى المذكور بقوله: "إذ يقول لصاحبه" والصاحب كان أبا بكر فكانت السكينة من الله تعالى نازلة عليه، إذ هو الذي كان يحزن، وإنزال السكينة تكون على من كانت السكينة زائلة عنه لا على من كانت سكينته قائمة. وفي الآية أنه ثاني النبي عليه السلام في الغار، وهو المختار لصحبته، ومثل هذه الخاصيات لم تثبت لأحد من الصحابة وإن جل قدره وعظمت منزلته. ثم إنه كان أول الرجال الأحرار إسلاما بلا خلاف بين الأمة، فإن الناس وإن اختلفوا في ذلك فقال بعضهم: زيد بن حارثة وكان أول الناس إسلاما، ومنهم من قال: كانت خديجة بنت خويلد، ومنهم من قال: بل كان علي أول الناس إسلاما، ومنهم من قال: كان أبو بكر الصديق أول الناس إسلاماً وعليه الأكثر، وقد قدم حسان بن ثابت إسلام أبي بكر في شعره وأنشده على رؤوس الأشهاد منهم المهاجرون الأولون ولم ينكر عليه أحد فقال: إذا تذكرت شجوا من أخي ثقة فاذكر أخاك أبا بكر بما فعلا خير البرية أتقاها وأعدلها بعد النبي وأوقاها بما حملا الصادق الثاني المحمود سيرته وأول الناس منهم صدق الرسلا وعلى قضية هذا قال أهل العلم: إن من صدق محمدًا عليه السلام بالرسالة ينال أبو بكر له مثل ثوابه، لأن النبي عليه السلام قال: من سن سنة حسنة فله أجرها وأجر من عمل بها إلى يوم القيامة، وأبو بكر هو الذي سن السنة.
The evidences for the superiority of al-Siddiq: “If you do not support him, Allah has already supported him when those who disbelieved drove him out, the second of two, when they were in the cave, when he said to his companion, ‘Do not grieve; indeed Allah is with us.’ And Allah sent down His tranquility upon him” (Surah al-Tawbah 9:40). In the verse, it is that he is the companion of the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him, and that Allah supported him as He supported His Prophet, where He said “Indeed Allah is with us,” i.e., with support. Then the pronoun in His saying “And Allah sent down His tranquility upon him” refers to the one mentioned in His saying “when he said to his companion,” and the companion was Abu Bakr, so the tranquility from Allah Most High was sent down upon him, because he was the one who was grieving, and the sending down of tranquility is upon the one from whom tranquility has departed, not upon the one whose tranquility is firm. And in the verse, it is that he is the second of the Prophet peace be upon him in the cave, and he is the chosen one for his companionship, and such special characteristics have not been established for any of the Companions, even if his rank is great and his station is exalted. Then indeed he was the first of free men to accept Islam without disagreement among the community, for people differed about that: some said Zayd ibn Haritha was the first to accept Islam, some said Khadija bint Khuwaylid, some said Ali was the first to accept Islam, and some said Abu Bakr al-Siddiq was the first to accept Islam, and the majority are upon this. And Hassan ibn Thabit presented Abu Bakr's Islam in his poetry and recited it before witnesses, including the first Muhajirun, and no one objected to him. He said: When I recall a sorrow from a trustworthy brother, then remember your brother Abu Bakr for what he did. The best of creation, most God-fearing, most just, after the Prophet, and most protective of what he bore. The truthful second, praised his conduct, and the first of people to believe in the Messenger. And based on this, the scholars said: Whoever affirms Muhammad's message, Abu Bakr obtains a reward like his reward, because the Prophet peace be upon him said: “Whoever sets a good precedent (sunna hasana) will have its reward and the reward of those who act upon it until the Day of Judgment.” And Abu Bakr is the one who set the precedent.
Source pages p. 1186

Commentary
This passage presents the evidence for the superiority of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The author first cites the Quranic verse (9:40) about the hijra and the cave. He interprets the verse to show that Abu Bakr is explicitly called 'the companion' (sahib) of the Prophet, and that Allah sent down tranquility (sakina) upon him because he was the one grieving. The author argues that the pronoun in 'upon him' refers back to the companion (Abu Bakr), not the Prophet, since the Prophet's tranquility was already firm. This unique companionship and the specific mention of tranquility are special honors not given to any other Companion. Then he notes that Abu Bakr was the first free man to accept Islam, according to the majority. To support this, he quotes a poem by Hassan ibn Thabit, recited publicly without objection, which praises Abu Bakr as the first to believe in the Messenger. Finally, the author cites the hadith that whoever sets a good precedent gets the reward of all who follow it, implying that Abu Bakr's early conversion set a precedent that earns him the reward of all who follow him. Thus, these arguments collectively establish Abu Bakr's superiority over all other Companions.

Key Terms
الصديق
صاحب
السكينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse only shows Abu Bakr was a companion, not necessarily superior.
Correction: The author argues that the specific mention of tranquility being sent down on him, and the unique companionship, indicate his superiority.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the phrase 'upon him' refer to Abu Bakr and not the Prophet?
A) Because the Prophet did not need tranquility
B) Because Abu Bakr was the one grieving
C) Both A and B
D) It is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
The cave verse uniquely singles out Abu Bakr as the recipient of divine tranquility and the chosen companion, establishing his superiority over all other Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials that cause you grief, do you truly believe that Allah's tranquility is sent specifically to the one who needs it, as it was sent to Abu Bakr? How can you actively seek that tranquility in your current struggles?
?
The Prophet chose Abu Bakr as his sole companion in the cave. Who are the people you have chosen to stand with you in your most difficult moments? Are you that kind of loyal supporter for someone else, or do you distance yourself when hardship comes?
?
If you were in the cave, hearing 'Do not grieve, indeed Allah is with us,' would your heart be at peace, or would doubt still linger? What does your answer reveal about the depth of your tawakkul (reliance on Allah)?

Historical Evidence: First Free Muslim and the Reward of Setting a Precedent
Historical and hadith-based arguments for Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's status as the first free man to accept Islam and the hadith on setting a good precedent are used to prove his superiority.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's early Islam and the hadith on precedent make his reward incomparable.

After the Quranic evidence, the author turns to historical facts. He notes that Abu Bakr was the first free man to accept Islam according to the majority, and he cites a poem by Hassan ibn Thabit as corroboration. Finally, he invokes the hadith that whoever sets a good precedent earns the reward of all who follow it, implying that Abu Bakr's early conversion sets a rewarding precedent. This lesson examines these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus on first free Muslim
Read the passage where the author states that the majority consider Abu Bakr the first free man to accept Islam, despite differing opinions.
This is a historical claim that establishes precedence.
2
Analyze the poem by Hassan ibn Thabit
The poem is recited publicly and no one objects, confirming Abu Bakr's status as first believer.
The poem corroborates the historical record.
3
Learn the hadith on setting a good precedent
The Prophet said that whoever sets a good precedent gets its reward and the reward of those who follow it. Abu Bakr is said to be the one who set the precedent of faith.
This amplifies his reward exponentially.
4
Synthesize the arguments
Combine the historical fact, poetic witness, and prophetic hadith to see how they collectively support Abu Bakr's superiority.

Interpretation of the Sakina Verse: Abu Bakr in the Cave
Imam Nasafi interprets the verse of sakina in the cave as referring to Abu Bakr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Nasafi's exegetical argument that the tranquility mentioned in the cave verse was sent down upon Abu Bakr, not the Prophet.

Core Idea
The pronoun in 'sent down His tranquility upon him' refers to Abu Bakr, not the Prophet.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi unpacks the verse of the cave (Surah Tawbah 9:40) to defend the unique status of Abu Bakr. He focuses on the pronoun reference and the logic of when tranquility is sent down. This lesson will walk through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Notice the key terms 'sakina', 'companion', and 'cave'.
2
Identify the pronoun referent
Identify the pronoun 'him' in the verse. Nasafi argues it refers to the companion, not the Prophet. Note the linguistic clue: the preceding phrase 'when he said to his companion'.
3
Understand the logic of sending down tranquility
Nasafi explains that tranquility is sent down upon one who is sad and has lost tranquility. The Prophet had innate tranquility, so the verse must refer to Abu Bakr, who was sad.
4
Appreciate the unique distinction
Nasafi concludes that being the second in the cave and chosen for companionship is a unique distinction for Abu Bakr, not shared by any other Companion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالنصر، ثم الهاء في قوله : فأنزل الله سكينته عليه عائدة إلى المذكور بقوله: "إذ يقول لصاحبه" والصاحب كان أبو بكر فكانت السكينة من الله تعالى نازلة عليه، إذ هو الذي كان يحزن، وإنزال السكينة تكون على من كانت السكينة زائلة عنه لا على من كانت سكينته قائمة. وفي الآية أنه ثاني النبي عليه السلام في الغار، وهو المختار لصحبته، ومثل هذه الخاصيات لم تثبت لأحد من الصحابة وإن جل قدره وعظمت منزلته
With victory, then the pronoun in His saying 'Then Allah sent down His tranquility upon him' refers to the one mentioned in His saying 'When he said to his companion' and the companion was Abu Bakr. So the tranquility from Allah was descending upon him, because he was the one who was sad, and the sending down of tranquility is upon one from whom tranquility had departed, not upon one whose tranquility was established. And in the verse, he is the second of the Prophet peace be upon him in the cave, and he is the chosen one for his companionship, and such characteristics have not been established for any of the Companions, however great his rank and exalted his station.
Source pages p. 1187

Commentary
This passage is an exegetical argument from the verse of the cave (Surah Tawbah 9:40). The author explains that the pronoun 'him' in 'sent down His tranquility upon him' refers to the companion mentioned in the verse, who is Abu Bakr, not the Prophet. He argues that tranquility was sent down upon Abu Bakr because he was sad, whereas the Prophet had tranquility already. Then he notes that the verse establishes Abu Bakr as the second of the two in the cave, chosen for companionship, and such a distinction is unique to him among the Companions.

Key Terms
السكينة (tranquility)
الغار (cave)
الصاحب (companion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the tranquility was sent down upon the Prophet.
Correction: The verse's pronoun refers to the companion (Abu Bakr), as argued by Imam Nasafi.

Checkpoint
According to the author, on whom did Allah send down His tranquility in the cave verse?
A) The Prophet
B) Abu Bakr
C) Both
D) The Prophet's family

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi argues that the tranquility in the cave verse was sent down on Abu Bakr, not the Prophet, based on pronoun reference and the logic of tranquility descending on the sad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the phrase 'He said to his companion, do not grieve' (9:40), do you automatically assume the comfort is for the Prophet, or do you pause to examine the words carefully? What does your default assumption reveal about how you approach Quranic interpretation?
?
Nasafi argues that tranquility descends only on the sad, not the already tranquil. In your own life, where do you seek tranquility — from your own strength or from realizing that Allah sends it precisely when you are weak?
?
If Abu Bakr's unique status in this verse were widely understood, would it change how you view the Companions? Are you willing to adjust your understanding of Islamic history based on precise textual evidence, even if it challenges popular narratives?

The First Free Adult Male Muslim: Consensus and Evidence
Nasafi establishes Abu Bakr's precedence as first free adult male Muslim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical consensus that Abu Bakr was the first free adult male Muslim and the evidence used to support it.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's precedence is established by consensus and confirmed by public testimony.

Imam Nasafi begins by addressing a debated historical point: who was the first Muslim? He clarifies the categories and shows that among free adult men, Abu Bakr is unanimously recognized as the first. He then presents a famous poem recited openly without objection as supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Abu Bakr's precedence
Read the Arabic passage that states Abu Bakr was the first free adult male Muslim without dispute. Note the mention of different opinions and the majority view.
The author acknowledges differing views but asserts consensus.
2
Understand the categories of 'first'
Notice that the disagreement is about first overall, but the author narrows it to free adult men. This clarifies the positions of Zayd (slave/freed), Khadijah (woman), Ali (child), and Abu Bakr (free adult male).
This categorization resolves the apparent contradictions.
3
Examine the poetic testimony
Read Hassan ibn Thabit’s poem and note that it was recited before the early Muhajirun with no objection. This public acceptance serves as strong evidence.
The poem explicitly names Abu Bakr as the first to believe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه كان أول الرجال الأحرار إسلاما بلا خلاف بين الأمة، فإن الناس وإن اختلفوا في ذلك فقال بعضهم: زيد بن حارثة وكان أول الناس إسلاما، ومنهم من قال: كانت خديجة بنت خويلد، ومنهم من قال : بل كان علي أول الناس إسلاما، ومنهم من قال : كان أبو بكر الصديق أول الناس إسلاماً وعليه الأكثر، وقد قدم حسان بن ثابت صل الله إسلام أبي بكر في شعره وأنشده على رؤوس الأشهاد منهم المهاجرون الأولون ولم ينكر عليه أحد فقال: إذا تذكرت شجوا من أخي ثقة فاذكر أخاك أبا بكر بما فعلا خير البرية أتقاها وأعدلها بعد النبي وأوقاها بما حملا الصادق الثاني المحمود سيرته وأول الناس منهم صدق الرسلا. وعلى قضية هذا قال أهل العلم : إن من صدق محمدًا عليه السلام بالرسالة ينال أبو بكر له مثل ثوابه، لأن النبي عليه السلام قال: من سن سنة حسنة فله أجرها وأجر من عمل بها إلى يوم القيامة وأبو بكر الله هو الذي سن السنة الحسنة، وهو تصديق رسول الله عليه السلام فيكون له مثل أجر من آمن به إلى يوم القيامة
Then indeed he was the first of free men to accept Islam without dispute among the community. For people, although they differed regarding that – some said: Zayd ibn Haritha was the first person to accept Islam, and among them some said: Khadijah bint Khuwaylid was, and among them some said: Rather Ali was the first person to accept Islam, and among them some said: Abu Bakr al-Siddiq was the first person to accept Islam, and the majority are upon that. And Hassan ibn Thabit presented Abu Bakr's Islam in his poetry and recited it in front of witnesses, including the early Muhajirun, and no one objected to him. He said: 'When you remember a pain from a trustworthy brother, remember your brother Abu Bakr for what he did. The best of creation, most pious and most just after the Prophet, and most cautious in bearing burdens, the truthful second, praised is his conduct, and the first of people to believe the messengers.' And upon this basis, the people of knowledge said: Whoever genuinely affirms Muhammad peace be upon him in his message, Abu Bakr attains the like of his reward, because the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever establishes a good practice, he has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it until the Day of Resurrection.' And Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) is the one who established the good practice, which is affirming the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him, so he has the like of the reward of everyone who believes in him until the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 1187

Commentary
This passage addresses the historical debate about who was the first to embrace Islam. The author states that Abu Bakr was the first free adult male Muslim without dispute. He lists the different opinions: Zayd ibn Haritha (first among slaves?), Khadijah (first among women), Ali (first among children), and the majority saying Abu Bakr was first among free men. He supports this with the testimony of Hassan ibn Thabit's poetry, which was recited publicly without objection. Then he applies the hadith about establishing a good practice: Abu Bakr's deed of being the first to sincerely believe in the Prophet is a good practice, so he earns the reward of all who follow that practice (i.e., all who believe in the Prophet after him). This is a theological argument for Abu Bakr's immense reward.

Key Terms
أول الرجال الأحرار
السنة الحسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Ali or Zayd was the first Muslim overall without considering categories.
Correction: Abu Bakr was the first free adult male Muslim; others were first in their own categories (women, children, slaves).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which category of 'first Muslim' does Abu Bakr belong to?
A) First of all people
B) First among free adult men
C) First among children
D) First among women

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr is unanimously recognized as the first free adult male Muslim, supported by poetic testimony from Hassan ibn Thabit accepted by the early companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recount your journey to faith, whose guidance do you acknowledge as instrumental? Are you as public and unwavering in your testimony as Hassan ibn Thabit was for Abu Bakr, even if it means potentially facing disagreement?
?
The early companions accepted the poem's claim without objection, showing their unity. Is there a matter of religious truth you are convinced of but hesitant to affirm publicly out of fear of discord? What would it take for you to speak up like the companions did?
?
Who in your life have you been slow to acknowledge as a blessing or a guide? Reflect on whether you are withholding recognition that could strengthen bonds, as the community did for Abu Bakr.

Abu Bakr's Reward: Establishing the Good Practice of Faith
Nasafi derives Abu Bakr's unique reward from the hadith on good practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's early and sincere belief entitles him to the reward of all believers until Judgment Day based on the hadith of establishing a good practice.

Core Idea
By being the first to believe, Abu Bakr established a good practice and earns its reward forever.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi builds on the historical fact of Abu Bakr's precedence to derive a profound theological reward. He connects Abu Bakr's act of being the first to affirm the Prophet's message with the prophetic hadith about establishing a good practice. This gives Abu Bakr a unique and immense reward that continues to grow until the end of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the reward theory
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'وعلى قضية هذا' to the end. Note how the author transitions from the historical fact to the theological conclusion.
The key is the application of the hadith 'من سن سنة حسنة'.
2
Identify the hadith quoted
Find the hadith: 'Whoever establishes a good practice, he has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it until the Day of Resurrection.' Understand its meaning.
This hadith is well-known and foundational for the concept of ongoing charity (sadaqah jariyah).
3
Connect Abu Bakr's action to the hadith
The author argues that Abu Bakr's action of being the first to sincerely affirm the Messenger is the 'good practice' (sunnah hasanah). Thus, everyone who believes after him follows this practice.
This makes Abu Bakr's reward continuous and immense.
4
Reflect on the scope of reward
Consider the implication: Abu Bakr receives the like of the reward of every believer until Qiyamah. This highlights his special status.
This is not a literal equal reward but a share of similar merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For people, although they differed regarding that – some said: Zayd ibn Haritha was the first person to accept Islam, and among them some said: Khadijah bint Khuwaylid was, and among them some said: Rather Ali was the first person to accept Islam, and among them some said: Abu Bakr al-Siddiq was the first person to accept Islam, and the majority are upon that. And upon this basis, the people of knowledge said: Whoever genuinely affirms Muhammad peace be upon him in his message, Abu Bakr attains the like of his reward, because the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever establishes a good practice, he has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it until the Day of Resurrection.' And Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) is the one who established the good practice, which is affirming the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him, so he has the like of the reward of everyone who believes in him until the Day of Resurrection.

B) Because he established the good practice of affirming the Messenger

?

?
Are you content to be a follower of the good practice established by Abu Bakr, or do you also strive to establish good practices for others in your community? What one specific good practice of faith can you establish this week that others might follow?
?
Knowing that your faith contributes to Abu Bakr's eternal reward, does that challenge your sense of ownership over your own good deeds? How can you transform that awareness into gratitude and action rather than jealousy or indifference?

Umar as a Good Deed of Abu Bakr and the Early Converts
Nasafi explains Umar as a good deed of Abu Bakr and lists early converts through him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi presents Umar as a good deed of Abu Bakr and lists the early converts who embraced Islam through Abu Bakr's influence.

Core Idea
Umar's greatness itself testifies to Abu Bakr's merit.

Imam Nasafi continues to extol Abu Bakr's virtues by asserting that even 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, despite his own towering status, is counted among the good deeds of Abu Bakr. He then clarifies the order of early converts and explains why Abu Bakr, more than others, became the model for the Muslim community. The passage provides a list of prominent Companions who accepted Islam through Abu Bakr's invitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the respectful language used for the Companions.
2
Identify the claim about Umar
Find the statement that Umar is a 'good deed' of Abu Bakr. Ask yourself what this implies about the relationship between the two.
3
Understand the cautious reconciliation
Note the phrase 'من تورع منهم' and how it presents the first believers by category. This resolves conflicting narrations.
This shows scholarly care in handling multiple reports.
4
Grasp why Abu Bakr is the model
Read the reasoning: people follow those of complete merits, intellect, and opinion. Understand why this elevates Abu Bakr's role.
5
Review the list of early converts
Identify the two groups of converts mentioned. Notice that Abu Bakr personally brought them to the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن هذا قالوا: إن عمر الله مع جلال قدره وكثرة مناقبه ومحله الشريف في الإسلام، كان حسنة من حسنات أبي بكر الصديق - رضي الله عنهما – ثم من تورع منهم فقال : أول من آمن بالنبي من النساء خديجة، ومن الصبيان علي ومن العبيد زيد بن حارثة ، ومن الرجال الأحرار أبو بكر الصديق - رضي الله عنهم أجمعين - ثم كيفما كان فهو المقتدى لغيره في الإسلام إذ الناس لا يقتدرون بالإناث والصبيان والعبيد إنما يقتدرون بمن تمت مناقبة، واشتهر بوفور العقل وكمال العلم وأصالة الرأي، ولهذا لم يقتد أحد بمن سوى أبي بكر الله في ذلك بل اقتدوا به حتى آمن يوم إسلامه أو غده: عثمان بن عفان، والزبير بن العوام، وطلحة بن عبيد الله وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص – رضي الله فجاء بهم إلى رسول الله الله فعرض عليهم الإسلام، وقرأ عليهم القرآن فآمنوا به وصدقوا برسالته وقيل لما أسلم أبو بكر وانصرف من عند رسول الله راح عليه بعثمان بن عفان ولطلحة بن عبيد الله والزبير بن العوام وسعد بن أبي وقاص، ثم جاء الغد بعثمان بن مظعون وبأبي عبيدة بن الجراح، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وبأبي سلمى بن الأسد والأرقم بن أبي الأرقم - رضي عنهم
And upon this they said: Indeed Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), despite his great rank, numerous merits, and noble status in Islam, was one of the good deeds of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq – may Allah be pleased with them both. Then among them who was cautious said: The first to believe in the Prophet among women was Khadijah, among children was Ali, among slaves was Zayd ibn Haritha, and among free men was Abu Bakr al-Siddiq – may Allah be pleased with them all. Then however it may be, he is the model for others in Islam, because people do not take example from women, children, and slaves; rather they take example from one whose merits are complete, renowned for abundant intellect, perfection of knowledge, and soundness of opinion. Therefore no one took example from anyone other than Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) in that matter, but rather they followed him. So on the day of his Islam or the next day, the following believed: Uthman ibn Affan, al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam, Talhah ibn Ubayd Allah, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas – may Allah be pleased with them. He brought them to the Messenger of Allah, who presented Islam to them and recited the Quran to them, so they believed in him and affirmed his message. And it is said: When Abu Bakr became Muslim and returned from the Messenger of Allah, he went to Uthman ibn Affan, Talhah ibn Ubayd Allah, al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. Then the next day he came with Uthman ibn Maz'un, Abu Ubaydah ibn al-Jarrah, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Abu Salmah ibn al-Asad, and al-Arqam ibn Abi al-Arqam – may Allah be pleased with them.
Source pages p. 1188

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of Abu Bakr's merits. It states that even the great Umar is considered a 'good deed' (hasana) of Abu Bakr, meaning his conversion and subsequent achievements are part of the reward for Abu Bakr's precedent. Then it presents a cautious view that reconciles the different 'firsts' by category. The author then explains why Abu Bakr is the model: people follow mature, intelligent, knowledgeable leaders, not women, children, or slaves. So Abu Bakr's conversion had the greatest impact. He then lists the early converts who embraced Islam through Abu Bakr, either on the same day or the next day, including prominent Companions.

Key Terms
حسنة
المقتدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Umar's conversion diminishes Abu Bakr's status or that the first converts were random.
Correction: This passage shows that Umar's virtue is actually a testament to Abu Bakr's merit, and the early converts were methodically brought by Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why was Abu Bakr the model for Islam rather than others?
A) Because he was the wealthiest
B) Because he had complete merits and sound intellect
C) Because he was the oldest
D) Because he was a relative of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's role as the model for early Muslims is affirmed by the fact that many prominent Companions embraced Islam through him, and even Umar's greatness is counted among his good deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even Umar's greatness is considered a 'good deed' of Abu Bakr, then who are the people whose influence has shaped your own faith? Are you living in such a way that your spiritual progress becomes a 'good deed' for those who guided you?
?
The passage says people emulate those of 'complete virtue, abundant intellect, and soundness of opinion.' In your daily life, whom are you emulating? Is your example leading others toward or away from the Prophet's way?
?
Abu Bakr brought people to Islam by personal invitation. Whom have you personally brought closer to faith, or are you content to let others do the work? What concrete step will you take this week to become a 'model' for someone else, even in a small way?

Abu Bakr's Steadfastness and Actions as Evidence of His Superiority
Description of Abu Bakr's steadfastness and actions after the Prophet's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's personal qualities and decisive actions during the crisis after the Prophet's death demonstrate his superiority over the other Companions.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's calm intellect and firm actions saved the Muslim community and proved his excellence.

This passage examines the first set of proofs for Abu Bakr's superiority. It highlights his unshakable composure when others panicked, his wisdom in sending Usama's army despite opposition, and his decisive action against apostasy. These deeds reveal his unique leadership and merit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get familiar with the content and the flow of the argument.
2
Identify Abu Bakr's qualities
Notice the qualities attributed to Abu Bakr at the beginning: strength of intellect, correct planning, calmness, bravery, and disregard for blame.
These set the foundation for his later actions.
3
Contrast with the Companions' confusion
Compare Abu Bakr's firmness with the confusion of the other Companions after the Prophet's death. Some denied the death, others claimed he was alive.
The contrast highlights Abu Bakr's superiority.
4
Note his three decisive actions
Identify the three actions: reciting the Quranic verse, dispatching Usama's army, and fighting apostates and zakat-withholders.
Each action required courage and wisdom.

على قوة عقله، وإصابة تدبيره، ورباطة جأشه، وغاية شجاعته، وقلة مبالاته بلومة اللائمين، فإن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كانوا لما حزبهم الأمر العظيم والخطب الهائل الجليل بوفاة رسول الله تحيروا في ذلك، حتى كان منهم من أنكر موته كراهة شق عصا المسلمين وتفرق كلمتهم، ومنهم من ادعى حياته عليه السلام لما ظن أنه لا يموت إذ هو خاتم الأنبياء، فهو عند ذلك ثبت قلبه ولم يتحير في أمره، وما ذهل عن رأيه عند نزول الخطب الذي لمثله يكترث ولدى حلوله إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ثم أنفذ جيش أسامة على خوف المسلمين التفرق والانقلاب وقال: لا أحل لواء عقده رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم إنه فعل ما فعل بأهل الردة وبمانعي الزكاة فهدى الله تعالى ببركة سعيه العرب بعدما نكصوا عن الدين على أعقابهم وارتدوا على أدبارهم، والله الموفق. وكذا تفويض النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر الصلاة إليه مع قوله عليه السلام: يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله تعالى الحديث، دل أنه كان أفضلهم، ولهذا قال له علي لما قال: أقيلوني فقام علي فقال: لا نقيلك ولا نستقيلك قدمك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نؤخرك رضيك لديننا فرضيناك لدنيانا وكذا لما قال أبو سفيان لعلي حين بويع أبو بكر: ما بال هذا الأمر في أذل قبيلة من قريش، لو شئت ملأتها عليهم خيلاً ورجالاً قال له علي: طال ما عاديت الإسلام وأهله أنا وجدتها أبا بكر لها أهلاً فهذه الدلائل تدل على كونه أفضل الصحابة، والله الموفق.
Upon his strength of intellect, correctness of planning, calmness of composure, utmost bravery, and lack of concern for the blame of blamers. For the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, when the great matter and the tremendous, grave calamity of the death of the Messenger of Allah befell them, they were confounded therein, to the extent that among them were those who denied his death out of dislike for splitting the staff of the Muslims and dispersing their word, and among them were those who claimed his life, peace be upon him, because they thought that he would not die since he is the Seal of the Prophets. But he (Abu Bakr), at that time, his heart was firm and he was not confounded in his affair, nor was he distracted from his opinion at the occurrence of the calamity, the like of which causes distress and at the time of its descent: 'Indeed, you are to die, and indeed, they are to die' [Quran 39:30]. Then he dispatched the army of Usama despite the Muslims' fear of division and reversal, and said: 'I will not untie a banner tied by the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him.' Then he did what he did with the people of apostasy and those who withheld zakat, so Allah guided, by the blessing of his effort, the Arabs after they had retreated from the religion on their heels and apostatized on their backs. And Allah is the Grantor of success. Likewise, the Prophet's, peace and blessings be upon him, entrusting the matter of prayer to him along with his saying, peace be upon him: 'Let the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead you in prayer' – the hadith – indicated that he was the most excellent of them. For this reason, Ali said to him when he (Abu Bakr) said: 'Relieve me' – then Ali stood and said: 'We will not relieve you nor seek relief from you; the Messenger of Allah put you forward, we will not put you back; he approved you for our religion, so we approve you for our worldly affairs.' Likewise, when Abu Sufyan said to Ali when Abu Bakr was pledged allegiance: 'What is this matter in the lowest tribe of Quraysh? If you wish, I will fill it against them with cavalry and men.' Ali said to him: 'Long have you been hostile to Islam and its people; I found Abu Bakr worthy of it.' So these evidences indicate that he is the most excellent of the Companions. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1191

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument for the superiority (afḍaliyya) of Abu Bakr over all other Companions, drawing on three categories of evidence: his personal qualities and actions, his appointment by the Prophet, and the recognition of his peers. The author begins with a description of Abu Bakr's steady character—strength of intellect, correct planning, calmness, bravery, and indifference to blame. Then he contrasts this with the confusion of the Companions after the Prophet's death. Some denied the death out of fear of division; some claimed he was still alive. Abu Bakr, however, remained firm, citing the Quranic verse 'Indeed, you are to die...' (39:30). Next, the author cites Abu Bakr's decisive actions: sending Usama's army despite fears, and fighting apostates and zakat-withholders, which restored the Arabs to Islam. The second piece of evidence is the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr, combined with the hadith 'يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله' (Let the most reciter lead you), showing Abu Bakr's precedence. The passage then records Ali's statement when Abu Bakr offered to resign: 'We will not relieve you... he approved you for our religion, so we approve you for our worldly affairs.' This indicates Ali's own recognition of Abu Bakr's worth. Finally, the author cites Abu Sufyan's objection and Ali's response that he found Abu Bakr worthy. The conclusion is that these evidences prove Abu Bakr is the best of the Companions.

Key Terms
أفضلية
الصحابة
أبو بكر
الردة
الزكاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr's superiority was based solely on his age or early conversion.
Correction: This passage shows his superiority was proven by his calm intellect, wise actions, and decisive leadership during the crisis.

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr do when some Companions denied the Prophet's death?
A) He argued with them.
B) He recited the Quranic verse 'Indeed, you are to die...'.
C) He called for a meeting.
D) He asked for help from the Muhajirun.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's steadfastness and decisive actions after the Prophet's death prove his superior intellect and leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a crisis that shakes your faith, do you hold firm to what you know is true, or do you let confusion and fear dictate your response? Abu Bakr recited the Quran and acted decisively. What verse or action will you cling to when your own calamity comes?
?
Abu Bakr did not care about the blame of blamers when he made difficult decisions. Is there a situation in your life where you remain silent or bend to avoid criticism, even though you know the right course? What would it cost you to act like Abu Bakr?
?
If you were among the Companions who denied the Prophet's death because it felt too painful, would you have had the honesty to accept the truth when Abu Bakr recited the verse? Where in your life today are you avoiding an uncomfortable truth about your own mortality or responsibilities?

The Prophetic Appointment and Companions' Recognition of Abu Bakr's Superiority
Evidence from Prophetic appointment and Companion testimonies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's delegation of prayer leadership to Abu Bakr and the statements of Ali and Abu Sufyan confirm Abu Bakr's superiority.

Core Idea
The Prophet chose Abu Bakr to lead prayer, and Ali confirmed his worth, establishing his excellence.

This lesson examines the second set of proofs: the Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr as prayer leader, which according to the hadith indicates his superior recitation and knowledge. Additionally, the testimony of Ali after the Prophet's death and his response to Abu Sufyan's objection demonstrate that the Companions themselves recognized Abu Bakr's superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the arguments presented.
2
Understand the prayer leadership argument
The Prophet entrusted prayer leadership to Abu Bakr, and the hadith 'Let the most reciter lead you' implies that the imam should be the most excellent. This indicates Abu Bakr's superiority.
This is a direct proof from the Prophet's action.
3
Analyze Ali's statement
When Abu Bakr offered to resign, Ali said 'We will not relieve you...' This shows Ali's recognition of Abu Bakr's worthiness.
Ali's testimony is significant as a leading Companion.
4
Examine Abu Sufyan's objection and Ali's response
Abu Sufyan criticized Abu Bakr's tribe, but Ali replied that he found Abu Bakr worthy of the caliphate.
This external testimony further confirms Abu Bakr's merit.

?

?

?
This passage shows that the Prophet's appointment is the ultimate endorsement. In what area of your life are you most resistant to accepting the guidance of the Prophet (peace be upon him) – whether in worship, relationships, or daily decisions – and why? Be honest: what would change if you fully embraced his choices?

Five Rafidi Proofs for Ali's Superiority
Lists the five Rafidi proofs for Ali's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five main arguments Rafidis use to claim Ali's superiority over the other Companions.

Core Idea
Rafidis rely on specific hadiths and historical claims to elevate Ali above all others.

Before refuting any argument, al-Nasafi first presents the Rafidi case in full. He lists five distinct proofs they use to assert Ali's superiority: the bird hadith, the brotherhood hadith, the city of knowledge, the most just judge, and Ali's unmatched bravery and pure monotheism. This lesson covers these claims without yet responding to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Rafidi arguments
Read the Arabic passage listing the five proofs. Notice how each one is introduced with a different expression like 'ما روى' or 'كذا يحتجون'.
The bird hadith is the first and longest proof.
2
Identify each proof
Make a mental list of the five proofs: (1) bird hadith, (2) brotherhood, (3) city of knowledge, (4) most just judge, (5) bravery and shirk-free life.
3
Understand the logic
For each proof, ask: How does this show Ali is superior? For example, the bird hadith implies he is the most beloved to Allah, thus the best.
This is the Rafidi interpretation; the author will later refute it.
4
Prepare for refutation
Notice that the passage ends with 'والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير...' — the refutation begins. This lesson only covers the arguments, not the response.
The full response is in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة الروافض على أفضلية علي والرد عليهم ثم عهدة ما تعلق الروافض به من تفضيل علي على غيره من الصحابة ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام قال: اللهم ائتني بأحب خلقك إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطير فجاءه علي له، فدل أنه أحب خلق الله إليه وأحبهم إليه أفضلهم، وكذا يحتجون بالمروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أخوه، وكذا يقولون: إنه كان أعلم الصحابة بدليل قوله عليه السلام: أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها وبدليل قوله عليه السلام: أقضاكم علي وكونه أشجع الناس لا ريب فيه، وكذا يتعلقون بكثرة جهاده وقتله أعداء الله تعالى ولم يدانه في ذلك أحد من الصحابة، وكذا يقولون: إنه لم يشرك بالله طرفة عين بخلاف غيره. والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير أن هذه الرواية منحولة، والصحيح من الروايات أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: ائتني بأحب خلقك إلي هكذا حدثنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن نصر الجميلي بإسناد صحيح، ثم هو معارض بما هو أشهر منه روى عن النبي أنه قيل له: من أحب الناس إليك قال: عائشة قيل من الرجال قال: أبو بكر هو ما دل معناه بأحب خلقك إلى أن عند النقلة وهو ما
The proofs of the Rafidis for the superiority of Ali and the refutation of them. Then the attachment of the Rafidis to preferring Ali over other Companions includes what was narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'O Allah, bring to me the most beloved of Your creation to You to eat with me from this bird,' so Ali came to him, so it indicated that he was the most beloved of Allah's creation to Him, and the most beloved of them to Him is the most excellent. Likewise, they argue by what is narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, was his brother. And likewise, they say that he was the most knowledgeable of the Companions by the evidence of his saying, peace be upon him: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and by the evidence of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The most just judge among you is Ali.' And that he was the bravest of people without doubt. Likewise, they cling to his abundant jihad and his killing of the enemies of Allah, and none of the Companions equaled him in that. And likewise, they say that he never associated anything with Allah even for a blink of an eye, unlike others. The answer to their attachment to the hadith of the bird is that this narration is fabricated, and the correct among the narrations is that he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me' – this is how our teacher Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Jamili narrated to us with a sound chain. Then it is countered by what is more famous than it: narrated from the Prophet that it was said to him: 'Who is the most beloved of people to you?' He said: 'Aisha.' It was said: 'From the men?' He said: 'Abu Bakr.' This is what its meaning indicates: 'the most beloved of Your creation to You' that, according to the transmitters, and what...
Source pages p. 1191

Commentary
This passage is a two-part presentation: first, the Rafidi (Shiite) arguments for Ali's superiority over other Companions; second, the author's refutation of the first argument (the bird hadith). The author begins by listing five Rafidi proofs: (1) The hadith of the bird: the Prophet asks Allah to bring the most beloved creation to eat with him, and Ali comes, so he is the most beloved and thus the best. (2) The hadith of brotherhood: the Prophet declared Ali his brother. (3) The hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' implying Ali's supreme knowledge. (4) The hadith 'The most just judge among you is Ali,' indicating his excellence in judgment. (5) Ali's unmatched bravery, jihad, and the fact that he never committed shirk even for a moment. The author then refutes only the first proof (the bird hadith) in this passage. He declares it fabricated (manḥūla) and offers a sounder narration: the Prophet said 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me' – but this version does not specify Ali. Moreover, the authentic and more famous hadith states that when asked who is most beloved, the Prophet said 'Aisha' and then 'Abu Bakr.' This counter-narration shows that the most beloved creation is actually Aisha and Abu Bakr, not Ali. The passage ends abruptly, but the refutation implies that the Rafidi argument is invalid.

تفضيل علي
خبر الطير
أنا مدينة العلم
أقضاكم علي

Key Takeaway
The Rafidis use five specific hadiths and historical claims to argue that Ali is superior to all other Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read these Rafidi proofs, do you feel any emotional pull to defend your own group's position? What does that reaction reveal about your attachment to partisan narratives over truth?
?
The Rafidis use specific hadiths to build their case. Are you willing to examine the sources of your own deeply held beliefs with the same critical eye, even if it makes you uncomfortable?
?
Which of these five proofs do you find most persuasive to your heart, and why? What does that attraction tell you about your own desire for a particular narrative about the early Muslim community?

Refutation of the Bird Hadith
Refutes the Rafidi argument from the bird hadith by declaring it fabricated and citing counter-hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the Rafidi argument from the bird hadith by declaring it fabricated and citing stronger counter-narrations.

Core Idea
The bird hadith is fabricated and contradicted by the authentic hadith that Aisha and Abu Bakr are the most beloved.

After listing the Rafidi proofs, the author begins his refutation with the first and most prominent: the hadith of the bird. He dismisses it as fabricated and offers a more reliable version that does not mention Ali. He then brings an even more famous hadith where the Prophet explicitly names Aisha and Abu Bakr as the most beloved people. This lesson focuses on the refutation of this single argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage from 'والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير' to the end. Notice the author's strategy: he first declares the narration fabricated, then provides an alternative sound narration, and finally cites a counter-hadith.
The text is incomplete, but the main points are clear.
2
Analyze the refutation structure
Break it down: (1) 'هذه الرواية منحولة' – the hadith is fabricated. (2) The correct wording is 'ائتني بأحب خلقك إلي' without specifying Ali. (3) It is countered by the famous hadith where the Prophet says the most beloved are Aisha and Abu Bakr.
3
Understand the counter-argument
The authentic hadith about Aisha and Abu Bakr directly contradicts the Rafidi claim that Ali is the most beloved. This shows the bird hadith cannot be authentic.
The author does not need to refute the other arguments here.
4
Reflect on the author's method
Note that the author uses isnad criticism (declaring it fabricated) and textual comparison (a more famous hadith). This is a typical kalam approach.
The refutation is partial; other arguments remain unanswered in this passage.

أدلة الروافض على أفضلية علي والرد عليهم ثم عهدة ما تعلق الروافض به من تفضيل علي على غيره من الصحابة ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام قال: اللهم ائتني بأحب خلقك إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطير فجاءه علي له، فدل أنه أحب خلق الله إليه وأحبهم إليه أفضلهم، وكذا يحتجون بالمروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أخوه، وكذا يقولون: إنه كان أعلم الصحابة بدليل قوله عليه السلام: أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها وبدليل قوله عليه السلام: أقضاكم علي وكونه أشجع الناس لا ريب فيه، وكذا يتعلقون بكثرة جهاده وقتله أعداء الله تعالى ولم يدانه في ذلك أحد من الصحابة، وكذا يقولون: إنه لم يشرك بالله طرفة عين بخلاف غيره. والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير أن هذه الرواية منحولة، والصحيح من الروايات أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: ائتني بأحب خلقك إلي هكذا حدثنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن نصر الجميلي بإسناد صحيح، ثم هو معارض بما هو أشهر منه روى عن النبي أنه قيل له: من أحب الناس إليك قال: عائشة قيل من الرجال قال: أبو بكر هو ما دل معناه بأحب خلقك إلى أن عند النقلة وهو ما
The proofs of the Rafidis for the superiority of Ali and the refutation of them. Then the attachment of the Rafidis to preferring Ali over other Companions includes what was narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'O Allah, bring to me the most beloved of Your creation to You to eat with me from this bird,' so Ali came to him, so it indicated that he was the most beloved of Allah's creation to Him, and the most beloved of them to Him is the most excellent. Likewise, they argue by what is narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, was his brother. And likewise, they say that he was the most knowledgeable of the Companions by the evidence of his saying, peace be upon him: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and by the evidence of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The most just judge among you is Ali.' And that he was the bravest of people without doubt. Likewise, they cling to his abundant jihad and his killing of the enemies of Allah, and none of the Companions equaled him in that. And likewise, they say that he never associated anything with Allah even for a blink of an eye, unlike others. The answer to their attachment to the hadith of the bird is that this narration is fabricated, and the correct among the narrations is that he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me' – this is how our teacher Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Jamili narrated to us with a sound chain. Then it is countered by what is more famous than it: narrated from the Prophet that it was said to him: 'Who is the most beloved of people to you?' He said: 'Aisha.' It was said: 'From the men?' He said: 'Abu Bakr.' This is what its meaning indicates: 'the most beloved of Your creation to You' that, according to the transmitters, and what...
Source pages p. 1191

Commentary
This passage is a two-part presentation: first, the Rafidi (Shiite) arguments for Ali's superiority over other Companions; second, the author's refutation of the first argument (the bird hadith). The author begins by listing five Rafidi proofs: (1) The hadith of the bird: the Prophet asks Allah to bring the most beloved creation to eat with him, and Ali comes, so he is the most beloved and thus the best. (2) The hadith of brotherhood: the Prophet declared Ali his brother. (3) The hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' implying Ali's supreme knowledge. (4) The hadith 'The most just judge among you is Ali,' indicating his excellence in judgment. (5) Ali's unmatched bravery, jihad, and the fact that he never committed shirk even for a moment. The author then refutes only the first proof (the bird hadith) in this passage. He declares it fabricated (manḥūla) and offers a sounder narration: the Prophet said 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me' – but this version does not specify Ali. Moreover, the authentic and more famous hadith states that when asked who is most beloved, the Prophet said 'Aisha' and then 'Abu Bakr.' This counter-narration shows that the most beloved creation is actually Aisha and Abu Bakr, not Ali. The passage ends abruptly, but the refutation implies that the Rafidi argument is invalid.

Key Terms
خبر الطير
منحولة
أحب الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The bird hadith is authentic and proves Ali is the most beloved creation.
Correction: The author shows it is fabricated and that authentic hadiths point to Aisha and Abu Bakr as the most beloved.

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary response to the Rafidi use of the bird hadith?
A) He accepts it but reinterprets it.
B) He declares it fabricated and provides counter-hadiths.
C) He argues Ali did not actually eat the bird.
D) He says the hadith is weak but not false.

Key Takeaway
The refutation of the bird hadith relies on declaring it fabricated, correcting its wording, and citing a stronger hadith about Aisha and Abu Bakr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you present evidence for your beliefs, do you first verify the authenticity of your sources as the author does here? What fabricated 'evidences' might you be unintentionally relying on in your own life?
?
The author uses stronger evidence to correct a false claim. How often do you accept what you hear about others without checking the stronger evidence? Whose reputation have you damaged by relying on weak narrations?
?
The most beloved people to the Prophet are Aisha and Abu Bakr. How does this reality affect your heart when you think about these companions? Do you feel genuine love for them? If not, what needs to change?

Arguments of the Rawafid for Ali's Superiority
Lists the Rawafid's proofs for Ali's superiority over other companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six arguments used by the Rawafid to claim Ali's superiority over the other Companions.

Core Idea
The Rawafid use hadiths and claims to argue Ali is superior, but these require refutation.

The author lists the arguments that the Rawafid (a Shi'a group) use to assert that Ali ibn Abi Talib is superior to all other Companions. These arguments include specific hadiths and claims about Ali's knowledge, bravery, and purity of faith. Understanding these arguments is essential before the author refutes them in subsequent passages.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Note the repeated 'وكذا' which introduces each new argument.
The author is presenting these arguments for refutation, not endorsement.
2
Identify each of the six arguments
Look for the distinct proofs: hadith of the bird, brotherhood, city of knowledge, most judicious, bravery/jihad, and never committing shirk.
Write down each argument in your own words.
3
Reflect on the author's approach
Ask yourself: why does the author list these arguments without immediate critique?
This prepares the reader for the upcoming refutation.

ثم عهدة ما تعلق الروافض به من تفضيل علي على غيره من الصحابة ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام قال : "اللهم ائتني بأحب خلقك إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطير فجاءه علي له، فدل أنه أحب خلق الله إليه وأحبهم إليه أفضلهم، وكذا يحتجون بالمروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام (أخوه، وكذا يقولون: إنه كان أعلم الصحابة بدليل قوله عليه السلام ) أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها وبدليل قوله عليه السلام: "أقضاكم" "علي" وكونه أشجع الناس لا ريب فيه، وكذا يتعلقون بكثرة جهاده وقتله أعداء الله تعالى ولم يدانه في ذلك أحد من الصحابة، وكذا يقولون: إنه لم يشرك بالله طرفة عين بخلاف غيره.
Then the responsibility of what the Rawafid clung to regarding preferring Ali over other companions: what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O Allah, bring me the most beloved of Your creation to You to eat with me from this bird' and Ali came to him, so it indicates that he is the most beloved of Allah's creation to Him, and the most beloved of them to Him is the most virtuous. Likewise, they say: he never associated anything with Allah for the blink of an eye, unlike others.

This passage lists the main arguments used by the Rawafid (Shi'a) to assert the superiority of Ali ibn Abi Talib over all other companions. The author enumerates five proofs: (1) the hadith of the bird where Ali comes as the most beloved to Allah; (2) the hadith that the Prophet called Ali his brother; (3) the hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate' indicating Ali's superior knowledge; (4) the hadith 'the most judicious among you is Ali'; (5) Ali's unmatched bravery and jihad; and (6) the claim that Ali never committed shirk even for a moment, unlike others. The author presents these without comment here, preparing to refute them.

Refuting the Bird Hadith: Fabrication and Specificity
Refutes the bird hadith as fabricated and interprets it as specific.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Rawafid's use of the bird hadith by arguing it is fabricated and that even if authentic, it indicates a specific occasion, not general superiority.

Core Idea
The bird hadith is fabricated; even if authentic, it only shows temporal favor.

This lesson examines the author's refutation of a key Shia proof-text, the hadith of the bird. The author first challenges its authenticity, then provides a more reliable counter-narration, and finally interprets the phrase to show it refers to a specific need, not absolute rank. A Quranic analogy solidifies the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the author's initial claim: 'هذه الرواية منحولة'. Then identify the counter-hadith and the Quranic verse quoted.
The passage is dense; focus on the logical flow.
2
Identify the three refutation strategies
The author uses three main arguments: (1) the narration is fabricated, (2) a more famous hadith contradicts it, (3) even if authentic, it is specific to a situation. Find each in the text.
3
Analyze the Quranic analogy
The author quotes Quran 3:33 to show that 'chosen' can be limited to a specific time. Compare how this supports the interpretation of the bird hadith as particular.
Notice the word 'اصطفى' is used in both contexts.
4
Reflect on the intended audience
Consider that this refutation is directed at the Rawafid (a Shia group). How does the author's approach address their specific claim?
The author does not deny Ali's virtue, only the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير أن هذه الرواية منحولة، والصحيح من الروايات أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: ائتني بأحب خلقك إلي هكذا حدثنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن نصر الجميلي بإسناد صحيح ، ثم هو معارض بما هو أشهر منه روى عن النبي لو أنه قيل له: "من أحب الناس إليك قال: عائشة قيل من الرجال، قال أبو هاشم هو ما دل معناه بأحب خلقك إلى أن يأكل معي، وكذا هو تأويل ما رووا أي بأحب خلقك إليك أن يأكل معي، ولعله كان أحب الخلق أن يأكل مع النبي لمساس حاجته في تلك الحالة، على أنه كان أحب خلقه إليه بعد من تقدمه من الخلفاء الراشدين فكان المراد منه الخصوص عرف ذلك بما تقدم من الدلائل، ومثل هذا جائز قال الله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ اصْطَفَى ءَادَمَ وَنُوحًا وَعَالَ إبْرَاهِيمَ وَعَالَ عِمْرَانَ عَلَى الْعَلَمِينَ ولم يكن هؤلاء مصطفين على نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فكانت الآية مخصوصة، وكان معناه على عالمي زمانهم فكذا هذا
The answer to their clinging to the report of the bird: that this narration is fabricated, and the correct among the narrations is that he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me.' Thus narrated to us Sheikh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Jumayli with a sound chain. Then it is opposed by what is more famous than it: it is narrated from the Prophet that if it was said to him: 'Who is the most beloved of people to you?' he said: 'Aisha.' It was said: 'Among men?' He said: 'Abu Hashim.' That is what its meaning indicates: 'the most beloved of Your creation to you to eat with me.' Likewise, it is the interpretation of what they narrated, i.e., 'the most beloved of Your creation to you to eat with me.' And perhaps he was the most beloved of creation to eat with the Prophet due to the need of his situation at that time. Rather, he was the most beloved of His creation to Him after those who preceded him among the Rightly Guided Caliphs. So what was intended was specificity, as known from the previous evidences. And such is permissible. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam and Noah and the family of Abraham and the family of Imran over the worlds.' And these were not chosen over our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), so the verse was specific, and its meaning was over the people of their time. So likewise this.
Source pages p. 1192

Commentary
This passage provides the author's refutation of the Rawafid's use of the hadith of the bird. The author argues: (1) The narration is fabricated (منحولة); the authentic version does not specify Ali. (2) The author cites a more famous hadith where the Prophet names Aisha and Abu Bakr as the most beloved. (3) The phrase 'most beloved to you to eat with me' indicates a specific occasion, not a general rank. (4) Even if Ali was the most beloved at that moment, it was due to a specific need. (5) Ali could be the most beloved after the earlier caliphs, so the hadith is limited. (6) The author draws an analogy with Quran 3:33 where the selection of certain families is specific to their time, not general. Thus, the Rawafid's argument fails.

Key Terms
منحولة
معارض
تأويل
خصوص
اصطفى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Rawafid believe the bird hadith proves Ali is the most beloved creation unconditionally and superior to all.
Correction: The author shows the narration is fabricated and even if authentic, it only indicates a temporary preference due to a specific need, not absolute superiority.

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary claim about the bird hadith narration?
A) It is weak but acceptable.
B) It is fabricated (منحولة).
C) It is authentic but misinterpreted.
D) It is stronger than the hadith about Aisha.

Key Takeaway
The bird hadith is fabricated, and even if authentic, its wording indicates a specific occasion, not general superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a weak or fabricated hadith because it supported a belief you were emotionally attached to? How does knowing that even the bird hadith is fabricated challenge you to be more rigorous in your own faith?
?
When you read the author's interpretation that Ali was the most beloved 'to eat with' the Prophet due to his need at that time, does that humbling explanation sit well with your heart? Or do you find yourself resisting it because you want Ali to be the best in an absolute sense?
?
The author uses a Quranic analogy (3:33) to show that 'chosen' can be specific to a time. Are you ready to accept that God's favor is not always what you imagined? How does this lesson force you to submit your own reasoning to the evidence, even when it deflates your preferred narrative?

Hadith Proving Abu Bakr's Superiority
Narrates a hadith stating Abu Bakr is the best of the Ummah after the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith narrated with a full chain is used as evidence for Abu Bakr's superiority over the rest of the Ummah after the Prophet.

Core Idea
Jibril's testimony makes Abu Bakr the best of the Ummah after the Prophet.

This lesson examines a key hadith that the author presents in his argument against the Rawafid. The hadith, with a detailed chain of transmission, recounts that during a sermon, the Prophet turned and did not see Abu Bakr, whereupon he announced that Jibril had just informed him that Abu Bakr is the best of the Ummah after him. This direct divine confirmation provides a strong doctrinal foundation for Abu Bakr's status.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its chain
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the lengthy chain of transmitters from the author back to the companion who witnessed the event.
The chain includes many scholars, showing the care in transmission.
2
Identify the prophetic statement
Find the exact words of the Prophet regarding Abu Bakr's status and note the source of the information: Jibril.
3
Understand the context
Recognize that this hadith is used in a sectarian debate to counter claims of Ali's superiority and establish the proper ranking of the companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودلائل الخصوص ما سبق وأحاديث كثيرة منها ما حدثنا القاضي الإمام أبو منصور بن أحمد العراقي قال : أخبرنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن محمد النجار الخطيب بسمرقند قال : أخبرنا أبو الحسن علي بن محمد السمرقندي قال : أخبرنا أبو بكر محمد أبو الفضل المفسر قال : أخبرنا أبو جعفر محمد بن الفضل بن أنيف العدل نا الرضي قال أخبرنا أحمد بن الليث بن الخليل الوراق قال : حدثنا النضر بن التيمي قال: حدثنا محمد بن موسى الأنصاري قاضي المدينة، وعبد الجبار بن سعد عن محمد بن عبد الملك بن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن زرارة عن أبيه عن جده قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يخطب فالتفت يمينا وشمالاً فلم ير أبا بكر فقال رسول الله عليه السلام أبو بكر ، أبو بكر، أما إن روح القدس جبريل عليه السلام أخبرني آنفًا أن خير أمتك بعدك أبو بكر
And evidences of specificity are what preceded and many hadiths, among them what narrated to us the Judge Imam Abu Mansur ibn Ahmad al-Iraqi said: informed us the Sheikh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Najjar al-Khatib in Samarqand said: informed us Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Samarqandi said: informed us Abu Bakr Muhammad Abu al-Fadl al-Mufassir said: informed us Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn al-Fadl ibn Anif al-Adl na al-Radi said: informed us Ahmad ibn al-Layth ibn al-Khalil al-Warraq said: narrated to us al-Nadr ibn al-Taymi said: narrated to us Muhammad ibn Musa al-Ansari, judge of Medina, and Abd al-Jabbar ibn Sa'd from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Zurara from his father from his grandfather said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) delivering a sermon, and he turned right and left and did not see Abu Bakr. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Abu Bakr, Abu Bakr. Indeed, the Holy Spirit Jibril (peace be upon him) informed me just now that the best of your Ummah after you is Abu Bakr.'
Source pages p. 1193

Commentary
This passage provides a hadith with a full chain of transmission to support the author's refutation of the Rawafid. The hadith reports that during a sermon, the Prophet noticed Abu Bakr was absent and declared that Jibril had just informed him that Abu Bakr is the best of his Ummah after him. This directly counters the Rawafid's claims of Ali's superiority. The lengthy chain demonstrates the author's care in citing an authentic source.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Hadith on Jibril Informing the Prophet of Abu Bakr's Virtue
Nasafi cites a hadith chain proving Abu Bakr's superiority after the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a specific hadith with a full chain to argue for Abu Bakr's virtue, and the importance of evaluating hadith chains in Sunni theology.

Core Idea
A single hadith with a verified chain establishes Abu Bakr as the best of the community after the Prophet.

In this passage, Nasafi presents a full hadith chain to support the Sunni position on the ranking of the Companions. He recounts a narrative where the Prophet, unable to see Abu Bakr during a sermon, announces that Gabriel has just informed him of Abu Bakr's supreme virtue. This lesson examines both the content of the hadith and the significance of its chain for establishing theological claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the chain of narrators (isnad) that precedes the main story.
The chain is long; don't skip it—it's crucial for authenticity.
2
Identify the key claim
Find the part where the Prophet states that Gabriel informed him that Abu Bakr is the best of the community after him. This is the doctrinal conclusion.
The phrase 'خير أمتك بعدك أبو بكر' is the core.
3
Analyze the chain's role
Consider why Nasafi includes the entire chain. How does the chain support the reliability of the report?
The chain connects the report to a Companion who witnessed the event.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Think about how this hadith defends the Sunni view of Abu Bakr's superiority over other Companions. How does it counter opposing views?
This is a key proof in Sunni kalam about the ranking of the Companions.

ومنها ما حدثنا القاضي الإمام أبو منصور بن أحمد العراقي قال : أخبرنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن محمد النجار الخطيب بسمرقند قال : أخبرنا أبو الحسن علي بن محمد السمرقندي قال: أخبرنا أبو بكر محمد أبو الفضل المفسر قال : أخبرنا أبو جعفر محمد بن الفضل بن أنيف العدل نا الرضي قال أخبرنا أحمد بن الليث بن خليل الوراق قال : حدثنا النضر بن التيمي قال: حدثنا محمد بن موسى الأنصاري قاضي المدينة، وعبد إبراهيم أسعد بن الجبار بن سعد عن محمد بن عبد الملك بن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن زرارة عن أبيه عن جده قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يخطب فالتفت يمينا وشمالاً فلم ير أبا بكر فقال رسول الله عليه السلام أبو بكر ، أبو بكر، أما إن روح القدس جبريل عليه السلام أخبرني آنفًا أن خير أمتك بعدك أبو بكر
Among them is what the judge Imam Abu Mansur ibn Ahmad al-Iraqi narrated to us: The Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Najjar al-Khatib in Samarqand informed us: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Samarqandi informed us: Abu Bakr Muhammad Abu al-Fadl al-Mufassir informed us: Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn al-Fadl ibn Anif al-Adl narrated to us from al-Radi, Ahmad ibn al-Layth ibn Khalil al-Warraq informed us: al-Nadr ibn al-Taymi narrated to us: Muhammad ibn Musa al-Ansari, judge of Madina, and Abd Ibrahim As'ad ibn al-Jabbar ibn Sa'd narrated to us from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Zurara, from his father, from his grandfather, who said: I saw the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, delivering a sermon and he turned right and left and did not see Abu Bakr. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Abu Bakr, Abu Bakr. Indeed, the Spirit of Holiness, Gabriel, peace be upon him, just informed me that the best of your community after you is Abu Bakr.'
Source pages p. 1193

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith with a full chain of transmission as evidence for Abu Bakr's superiority. The chain traces back to a companion who witnessed the Prophet inquiring about Abu Bakr and then announcing that Jibril (Gabriel) had informed him that Abu Bakr is the best of the community after the Prophet. The inclusion of the chain underscores the author's reliance on authentic transmitted reports (hadith) in defending the Sunni position on the virtues of the companions.
